 # GitLogs
 
-Auto-post your Git commits to X/Twitter with AI-generated changelogs. OAuth in, webhook in, Gemini-summarized tweet out.
+**Turn `git push` into a published changelog tweet.** Sign in with GitHub, link your X account, enable a repo — every push then fires a webhook, Gemini summarizes the real diff, and a changelog post lands on your own X timeline. No manual tweeting, no abandoned changelog.

-[![License](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-c8693d?style=flat)](LICENSE)

 ## Why
 
-Devs ship constantly but rarely tell anyone. Manual tweeting kills momentum; abandoned changelogs kill discoverability. GitLogs closes the loop — you push code, the world hears about it. Gemini turns raw diffs into reader-friendly prose; webhooks fire the whole thing on every commit.
+Developers ship constantly but rarely tell anyone. Manual tweeting kills momentum; abandoned changelogs kill discoverability. GitLogs closes the loop — you push code, the world hears about it. Gemini turns raw diffs into reader-friendly prose grounded in what actually changed, and webhooks fire the whole thing on every commit.
 
-## Features
+## See it in 30 seconds
 
-- **GitHub OAuth** — sign in once, link as many repos as you want
-- **Auto webhooks** — created automatically when you enable a repo
-- **AI changelogs** — Gemini-powered commit summaries
-- **Auto-post to X** — tweet commits without lifting a finger
-- **Threading** — chain related commits into a single thread
+There's a **keyless `/demo` route** — no GitHub, no X, no API keys. It replays bundled commit fixtures through the real pipeline shape entirely client-side: a commit + diff become an interpolated Gemini prompt, which becomes a generated changelog post. A persona toggle (Professional / Hype / Deadpan Technical) re-renders the prompt and output so you can see the prompt engineering, not just the result.
 
-## How it works
+Run it locally:
 
-1. Sign in with GitHub
-2. Connect your X/Twitter account
-3. Enable repos you want to track
-4. Push commits → webhook fires → Gemini summarizes → tweet posts
+```bash
+pnpm setup && pnpm dev:all
+# then open http://localhost:5173/demo
+```
 
-## Stack
+A hosted demo link is pending deployment — see the **Demo** badge above once it's live.
+
+### Example output
+
+A real generated post from the demo fixtures, for commit `a1b2c3d` on `octo-dev/payments-api` (`feat: idempotency keys on POST /charges`), in the **Professional** persona:
+
+> shipped: idempotency keys on POST /charges. retries now return the original charge instead of creating a duplicate. one required header, zero double-charges. (a1b2c3d)
+
+The same diff in **Deadpan Technical**:
+
+> POST /charges: require Idempotency-Key header (400 if missing). lookup by key first, return existing charge 200 if found, else create with key. backed by a partial unique index where key is not null. (a1b2c3d)
 
-**Frontend** — React · Vite
-**Backend** — Node.js · Express · SQLite
-**AI** — Google Gemini (changelog generation)
-**Auth** — GitHub OAuth2 · X OAuth2
+The prompt feeds Gemini the actual diff as ground truth and instructs it to describe only what changed — no hallucinated features.
+
+## How it works
+
+Every push hits `POST /webhook/github`. The backend verifies the GitHub HMAC signature (failing **closed** if no secret is configured — see [security](#configuration)), resolves which user owns the repo, and runs a two-stage AI pipeline per non-merge commit: Stage 1 fetches the real diff from the GitHub REST API and asks Gemini for a factual summary; Stage 2 feeds that grounded summary into the user's prompt template and posts the result to their own X account. Stage 2 runs through a rate-limited, retrying, restart-survivable queue backed by SQLite.
+
+```mermaid
+sequenceDiagram
+    autonumber
+    participant GH as GitHub
+    participant WH as webhookHandler
+    participant DA as diffAnalyzer
+    participant GEM as geminiClient
+    participant Q as queueService
+    participant DB as SQLite (sql.js)
+    participant TW as twitterClient / X
+
+    GH->>WH: POST push (raw body + x-hub-signature-256)
+    WH->>WH: HMAC-SHA256 verify (timingSafeEqual; fail CLOSED if no secret)
+    alt invalid or no secret
+        WH-->>GH: 401 reject
+    else valid
+        WH->>DB: resolve repo -> user -> X auth
+        loop each non-merge commit
+            WH->>DA: fetchCommitDiff(repo, sha)
+            DA-->>WH: diff + files + stats
+            WH->>GEM: analyzeDiff(diff) — Stage 1 (factual summary)
+            WH->>GEM: generateChangelog(commit, diffSummary) — Stage 2
+            GEM->>Q: enqueue task (persisted, rate-limited)
+            Q->>DB: saveQueueItem(pending)
+            Q->>GEM: run template + diffSummary through Gemini (retry w/ backoff)
+            GEM-->>WH: changelog text
+            WH->>TW: postTweet(text, optional quote)
+            TW-->>WH: tweet id
+            WH->>DB: saveTweetId(repo, sha, tweetId)
+        end
+        WH-->>GH: 200 { processed, total }
+    end
+```
+
+For the full sequence, OAuth flows, data model, and documented failure modes, see [`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`](docs/ARCHITECTURE.md).
 
 ## Quick start
 
+Requires **Node >= 18** and **pnpm**. Windows, macOS, and Linux are all supported (the codebase is developed on Windows). Lockfiles are committed (root + `frontend/`) for reproducible installs.
+
 ```bash
 git clone https://github.com/aayushman-singh/git-twitter-bot.git gitlogs
 cd gitlogs
-npm install
-cp .env.example .env   # fill in keys
-npm start
+
+pnpm setup            # install backend + frontend deps
+cp .env.example .env  # fill in your keys (see Configuration)
+pnpm seed             # populate a demo SQLite db with fixtures
+pnpm dev:all          # backend (nodemon) + Vite dev server together
 ```
 
+Then open the dashboard at `http://localhost:5173` or the keyless demo at `http://localhost:5173/demo`.
+
+```bash
+pnpm test             # run the Vitest backend suite
+pnpm build            # build the SPA to frontend/dist
+```
+
+## Stack
+
+| Layer | Tech |
+| --- | --- |
+| Frontend | React 18 · Vite 5 · PrimeReact · React Router |
+| Backend | Node.js · Express 4 |
+| Datastore | SQLite via [sql.js](https://sql.js.org) (WASM, single-file) |
+| AI | Google Gemini — two-stage diff analysis + changelog generation |
+| Auth | GitHub OAuth2 (login + webhook control) · X OAuth 2.0 with PKCE (posting) |
+
+The backend is a single Express process that also serves the built SPA from `frontend/dist` in production.
+
+## Configuration
+
+Copy `.env.example` to `.env` and fill in real values — every value in the example is a placeholder. The key groups:
+
+- **GitHub OAuth** — `GITHUB_CLIENT_ID`, `GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET` (create an OAuth app at github.com/settings/developers).
+- **Webhook secret** — `WEBHOOK_SECRET`. **Do not skip this.** Signature verification fails *closed*: with no secret configured, every incoming webhook is rejected rather than trusted. Generate one with `openssl rand -hex 20`.
+- **X OAuth 2.0** — `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` (required), `OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` (optional, enables confidential-client mode), `OAUTH_CALLBACK_URL`.
+- **Gemini** — `GEMINI_API_KEY`, `GEMINI_MODEL` (default in the example is `gemini-2.5-flash`). Get a key at aistudio.google.com/app/apikey.
+- **Server** — `PORT`, `FRONTEND_URL`, `API_BASE_URL`, `DATABASE_PATH`, `ADMIN_API_KEY` (gates the `/api/*` admin routes), plus optional queue/rate-limit tuning (`QUEUE_MAX_RPM`, `QUEUE_MAX_RETRIES`, ...).
+
 ## API
 
 | Method | Path | Purpose |
 | --- | --- | --- |
-| `GET` | `/auth/github` | Start GitHub OAuth |
-| `GET` | `/auth/x` | Start X/Twitter OAuth |
-| `POST` | `/webhook/github` | GitHub webhook receiver |
-| `GET` | `/api/me` | Current user |
-| `GET` | `/api/me/repos` | User repositories |
-| `GET` | `/api/health` | Health check |
-
-## Development
+| `GET` | `/auth/github` | Start GitHub OAuth login |
+| `GET` | `/auth/github/callback` | GitHub OAuth callback |
+| `GET` | `/auth/x` | Start X OAuth 2.0 PKCE flow (requires GitHub login) |
+| `GET` | `/auth/x/callback` | X OAuth callback |
+| `POST` | `/auth/logout` | Clear session + stored token |
+| `POST` | `/webhook/github` | GitHub push webhook receiver (HMAC-verified) |
+| `GET` | `/api/me` | Current user + X connection status |
+| `GET` | `/api/me/repos` | User repositories with enabled/OG status |
+| `POST` | `/api/me/repos/enable` | Enable a repo (creates the webhook) |
+| `POST` | `/api/me/repos/disable` | Disable a repo (removes the webhook) |
+| `GET` | `/api/me/templates` | List the user's prompt templates |
+| `GET` | `/api/health` | Health check (queue + feature flags) |
+| `GET` | `/api/stats` | Queue + system stats (admin, API-key gated) |
+
+## Testing
 
 ```bash
-npm run dev      # Hot reload
-npm run build    # Build frontend
+pnpm test        # one-shot Vitest run
+pnpm test:watch  # watch mode
 ```
 
+The backend suite (`tests/`) covers a **webhook end-to-end test** (`webhook.e2e.test.js`) — driving a signed push payload through the wired Express app via supertest — and the **queue mechanics** (`queue.test.js`): rate limiting, retry/backoff, and restart persistence.
+
+## Architecture
+
+A single Express process serves the React SPA, terminates both OAuth flows, verifies and processes webhooks, and persists everything to a single-file sql.js database. Full component map, sequence diagrams, ER model, and a candid list of known weaknesses live in [`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`](docs/ARCHITECTURE.md).
+
+## Contributing
+
+1. Fork the repo and create a branch off `main` (`feat/...`, `fix/...`).
+2. Make atomic commits with [Conventional Commit](https://www.conventionalcommits.org) messages (`feat:`, `fix:`, `docs:`, ...).
+3. Make sure `pnpm test` passes.
+4. Open a pull request describing the change and the user-facing impact.
+

+# RUNBOOK — gitlogs
+
+Operational guide for the **keyed production path** (the full product: GitHub
+OAuth, X OAuth, Gemini, live posting) and the **keyless demo deploy** (the
+public `/demo` showcase). Every secret below is templated — fill in your own.
+
+---
+
+## 0. Secret rotation (do this FIRST)
+
+The repository's history is clean of real secrets (`.env` was never committed;
+`.env.example` was scrubbed of the partial OAuth credentials it once held). But
+the live credentials that previously sat in a local `.env` should be treated as
+compromised and **rotated before any production deploy**:
+
+| Credential | Where to rotate |
+| --- | --- |
+| GitHub OAuth client secret | github.com/settings/developers → your OAuth app → "Generate a new client secret" |
+| X / Twitter OAuth2 client secret | developer.twitter.com → your app → Keys and tokens → regenerate |
+| X / Twitter API key/secret + access token/secret + bearer | same X app → regenerate all |
+| Gemini API key | aistudio.google.com/app/apikey → revoke + create new |
+| Cloudflare API token | dash.cloudflare.com → My Profile → API Tokens → roll |
+| `WEBHOOK_SECRET` | regenerate: `openssl rand -hex 20` (then update each repo's webhook) |
+| `ADMIN_API_KEY` | regenerate: `openssl rand -hex 32` |
+
+After rotating, put the new values **only** in the server's `.env` (git-ignored)
+and in your deploy provider's secret store. Never commit them.
+
+---
+
+## 1. Provision the integrations (one-time)
+
+1. **GitHub OAuth app** — github.com/settings/developers → New OAuth App.
+   - Homepage: `https://<your-frontend-domain>`
+   - Callback: `https://<your-api-domain>/auth/github/callback`
+   - Copy `GITHUB_CLIENT_ID` / `GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET`.
+2. **X (Twitter) app** — developer.twitter.com → Project → App with **OAuth 2.0**.
+   - Type: Web App / Confidential client.
+   - Callback: `https://<your-api-domain>/auth/x/callback`
+   - Scopes: `tweet.read tweet.write users.read offline.access`.
+   - Copy `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` / `OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` (+ the API keys/tokens).
+3. **Gemini** — aistudio.google.com/app/apikey → `GEMINI_API_KEY`.
+
+---
+
+## 2. Configure `.env`
+
+```bash
+cp .env.example .env
+```
+
+Fill in (see `.env.example` for the full annotated list):
+
+```ini
+NODE_ENV=production
+PORT=3000
+FRONTEND_URL=https://<your-frontend-domain>
+API_BASE_URL=https://<your-api-domain>
+
+GITHUB_CLIENT_ID=<rotated>
+GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET=<rotated>
+
+OAUTH_CLIENT_ID=<rotated>          # X OAuth2 client id
+OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET=<rotated>
+OAUTH_CALLBACK_URL=https://<your-api-domain>/auth/x/callback
+
+GEMINI_API_KEY=<rotated>
+GEMINI_MODEL=gemini-2.5-flash
+
+WEBHOOK_SECRET=<openssl rand -hex 20>   # REQUIRED — HMAC fails CLOSED without it
+ADMIN_API_KEY=<openssl rand -hex 32>
+DATABASE_PATH=./tweets.db
+ALLOWED_REPOS=                          # empty = accept all enabled repos
+```
+
+> **Fail-closed note:** with no `WEBHOOK_SECRET`, every incoming webhook is
+> rejected (401). This is intentional — a missing secret is a misconfiguration,
+> not a reason to trust unsigned payloads.
+
+---
+
+## 3. One-command server bring-up (EC2 / any Node host)
+
+```bash
+git clone https://github.com/aayushman-singh/git-twitter-bot.git ~/gitlogs
+cd ~/gitlogs
+corepack enable && corepack prepare pnpm@latest --activate   # if pnpm absent
+pnpm install --frozen-lockfile
+pnpm --dir frontend install --frozen-lockfile
+VITE_API_BASE=https://<your-api-domain> pnpm --dir frontend run build
+# (.env already in place from step 2)
+node src/server.js     # or via systemd, below
+```
+
+The backend serves the built SPA from `frontend/dist` and exposes the API +
+`/webhook/github` on `PORT`.
+
+### systemd unit (template)
+
+`/etc/systemd/system/gitlogs.service`:
+
+```ini
+[Unit]
+Description=gitlogs
+After=network.target
+
+[Service]
+Type=simple
+User=<deploy-user>
+WorkingDirectory=/home/<deploy-user>/gitlogs
+EnvironmentFile=/home/<deploy-user>/gitlogs/.env
+ExecStart=/usr/bin/node src/server.js
+Restart=on-failure
+RestartSec=5
+
+[Install]
+WantedBy=multi-user.target
+```
+
+```bash
+sudo systemctl daemon-reload
+sudo systemctl enable --now gitlogs
+sudo systemctl status gitlogs
+```
+
+---
+
+## 4. Continuous deploy (GitHub Actions → EC2)
+
+`.github/workflows/deploy-ec2.yml` SSHes in on push to `main`, pulls, installs
+from the frozen lockfiles, **builds the frontend**, and restarts the service.
+
+Required repo **Actions secrets** (Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions):
+
+| Secret | Value |
+| --- | --- |
+| `EC2_HOST` | server hostname / IP |
+| `EC2_USER` | ssh user (the systemd `User=`) |
+| `EC2_SSH_KEY` | private key authorized on the host |
+| `EC2_PORT` | ssh port (optional, defaults to 22) |
+
+Also set `VITE_API_BASE` in the deploy environment (or edit the workflow's
+default) so the SPA is built against the right API origin.
+
+> **Known tradeoff (codex review):** the workflow currently builds on the prod
+> host. For a hardened setup, build the SPA artifact in CI and ship only
+> `frontend/dist` to the host, so prod carries no dev/build toolchain. Tracked
+> as a follow-up; the current approach is fine for a single small instance.
+
+---
+
+## 5. DNS
+
+The historical hosts `gitlogs.aayushman.dev` / `api-gitlogs.aayushman.dev` are
+NXDOMAIN. Point:
+
+- `<your-frontend-domain>` → the host (or the static SPA deploy).
+- `<your-api-domain>` → the EC2 instance running the backend.
+
+Update the GitHub + X OAuth callback URLs and `.env` to match.
+
+---
+
+## 6. Keyless demo deploy (Vercel / Cloudflare Pages)
+
+The `/demo` route is fully client-side (no backend, no keys) — ideal for a
+static host. Because `frontend/src/utils/api.js` fails loudly in production
+builds when `VITE_API_BASE` is unset, pass a value at build time even though the
+demo never calls it.
+
+**Vercel** (root directory = `frontend/`):
+- Build command: `pnpm build`
+- Output dir: `dist`
+- Env: `VITE_API_BASE = https://<your-api-domain>` (or any placeholder)
+- `frontend/vercel.json` already provides the SPA rewrite so `/demo` deep-links.
+
+```bash
+# from the frontend/ directory, with the Vercel CLI authenticated:
+VITE_API_BASE=https://gitlogs.example pnpm build
+npx vercel deploy --prebuilt --prod   # or `npx vercel` and follow prompts
+```
+
+**Cloudflare Pages**:
+- Build command: `pnpm build`  · Output: `frontend/dist`  · Root: `frontend`
+- Or direct upload: `npx wrangler pages deploy frontend/dist`
+
+After deploying, update the **Demo** badge/link in `README.md` with the live URL.
+
+---
+
+## 7. Verify a deploy
+
+```bash
+curl -s https://<your-api-domain>/api/health        # → 200 JSON
+# Push a commit to an enabled repo, then check the X account + logs:
+sudo journalctl -u gitlogs -f
+```
+
+A correctly working pipeline logs: signature verified → repo/user resolved →
+diff fetched → Stage 1/2 Gemini → queued → posted tweet id → persisted.

+/**
+ * Self-contained demo fixtures for the keyless /demo route.
+ *
+ * These are fictional, deterministic examples drawn from fixtures/seed-data.json
+ * (octo-dev/payments-api, mira-builds/design-system, kai-ships/realtime-sync,
+ * nova-labs/ml-pipeline). They replay the gitlogs pipeline entirely client-side:
+ *
+ *   commit + diff  ->  interpolated Gemini prompt  ->  generated tweet thread
+ *
+ * No network calls. No backend. No PII. Everything renders offline.
+ *
+ * Each example exposes `promptTemplate(persona)` so the prompt card re-renders
+ * with the active persona's instruction line, mirroring the real
+ * "regenerate with a different persona" behaviour.
+ */
+
+const PERSONA_ORDER = ['professional', 'hype', 'technical'];
+
+/**
+ * Build the Gemini prompt that the backend would send for a given example and
+ * persona. The diff, commit, and repo context are interpolated in so viewers
+ * can see the prompt engineering, not just the output.
+ */
+function buildPrompt(example, persona) {
+  return `You are gitlogs, an AI that turns a git commit into a developer changelog post for X.
+
+PERSONA
+${persona.instruction}
+
+REPO CONTEXT
+- Repository: ${example.repoFullName}
+- Author: @${example.author}
+- Branch: ${example.commit.branch}
+- About: ${example.projectContext}
+
+COMMIT
+- SHA: ${example.commit.sha}
+- Message: ${example.commit.message}
+
+GIT DIFF (ground truth — describe ONLY what changed here, never invent)
+${example.diff}
+
+RULES
+- Each post is <= 280 characters.
+- Describe only changes evident in the diff above. No hallucinated features.
+- No hashtags. No emojis.
+- If the change is large, return a short thread (2-3 posts) instead of one post.
+- Match the PERSONA's voice exactly.
+
+Return the post(s) as the changelog, nothing else.`;
+}
+
+const rawExamples = [
+  {
+    id: 'payments-idempotency',
+    repoFullName: 'octo-dev/payments-api',
+    author: 'octo-dev',
+    avatarSeed: 'octo-dev',
+    projectContext:
+      'A payments service handling charges, refunds and webhooks. Node.js + Postgres ledger.',
+    commit: {
+      sha: 'a1b2c3d',
+      message: 'feat: idempotency keys on POST /charges',
+      branch: 'main',
+    },
+    diff: `diff --git a/src/routes/charges.js b/src/routes/charges.js
+index 4f1c2a0..9b7e3d1 100644
+--- a/src/routes/charges.js
++++ b/src/routes/charges.js
+@@ -12,9 +12,21 @@ router.post('/charges', async (req, res) => {
+-  const charge = await ledger.createCharge(req.body);
+-  res.status(201).json(charge);
++  const key = req.header('Idempotency-Key');
++  if (!key) {
++    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Idempotency-Key header required' });
++  }
++
++  const existing = await ledger.findChargeByKey(key);
++  if (existing) {
++    return res.status(200).json(existing);
++  }
++
++  const charge = await ledger.createCharge({ ...req.body, idempotencyKey: key });
++  res.status(201).json(charge);
+ });
+diff --git a/migrations/0007_idempotency.sql b/migrations/0007_idempotency.sql
+new file mode 100644
+index 0000000..a3f9c80
+--- /dev/null
++++ b/migrations/0007_idempotency.sql
+@@ -0,0 +1,3 @@
++ALTER TABLE charges ADD COLUMN idempotency_key TEXT;
++CREATE UNIQUE INDEX idx_charges_idem_key
++  ON charges (idempotency_key) WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;`,
+    personas: {
+      professional: {
+        thread: [

+export const PERSONA_LABELS = {
+  professional: { label: 'Professional', instruction: 'Sharp and factual. State what shipped and why it matters. No hype, no emojis, no hashtags.' },
+  hype: { label: 'Hype / Launch', instruction: 'High-energy launch voice. Lead with the win, sell the impact, keep it punchy. Still no emojis, still no hashtags.' },

+ * Each example, decorated with its persona definitions (label + instruction +
+ * thread) and a promptTemplate(persona) function bound to that example.

+export const DEMO_EXAMPLES = rawExamples.map((example) => {
+  const personas = {};

+    personas[key] = {
+      key,
+      label: PERSONA_LABELS[key].label,
+      instruction: PERSONA_LABELS[key].instruction,
+      thread: example.personas[key].thread,
+    };
+  }
+  return {
+    ...example,
+    personas,
+    promptTemplate: (persona) => buildPrompt(example, persona),
+  };
+});

+import { useMemo, useState } from 'react';
+import { Link } from 'react-router-dom';
+import { DEMO_EXAMPLES, PERSONA_KEYS } from '../demo/demoData';
+
+// Deterministic, dependency-free avatar: colored tile + initials derived from
+// the handle. Keeps the demo fully offline (no dicebear / external fetch).
+function avatarFor(seed) {
+  let hash = 0;
+  for (let i = 0; i < seed.length; i += 1) {
+    hash = (hash * 31 + seed.charCodeAt(i)) >>> 0;
+  }
+  const hue = hash % 360;
+  const parts = seed.split(/[-/]/).filter(Boolean);
+  const initials = (parts[0]?.[0] || seed[0] || '?').toUpperCase()
+    + (parts[1]?.[0] || parts[0]?.[1] || '').toUpperCase();
+  return {
+    initials,
+    background: `linear-gradient(135deg, hsl(${hue} 55% 32%), hsl(${(hue + 40) % 360} 60% 22%))`,
+  };
+}
+
+// Render a unified diff with +/- line colouring.
+function DiffView({ diff }) {
+  const lines = diff.split('\n');
+  return (
+    <pre className="demo-diff" aria-label="git diff">
+      <code>
+        {lines.map((line, i) => {
+          let cls = 'demo-diff-line';
+          if (line.startsWith('+') && !line.startsWith('+++')) cls += ' is-add';
+          else if (line.startsWith('-') && !line.startsWith('---')) cls += ' is-del';
+          else if (line.startsWith('@@')) cls += ' is-hunk';
+          else if (
+            line.startsWith('diff ')
+            || line.startsWith('index ')
+            || line.startsWith('+++')
+            || line.startsWith('---')
+            || line.startsWith('new file')
+          ) cls += ' is-meta';
+          return (
+            <span key={i} className={cls}>
+              {line || ' '}
+            </span>
+          );
+        })}
+      </code>
+    </pre>
+  );
+}
+
+function TweetCard({ example, thread }) {
+  const avatar = avatarFor(example.avatarSeed);
+  const displayName = example.author
+    .split(/[-/]/)
+    .map((p) => p.charAt(0).toUpperCase() + p.slice(1))
+    .join(' ');
+  return (
+    <div className="demo-thread" aria-label="generated changelog thread">
+      {thread.map((text, i) => (
+        <article className="demo-tweet" key={i}>
+          <div className="demo-tweet-avatar" style={{ background: avatar.background }} aria-hidden="true">
+            {avatar.initials}
+          </div>
+          <div className="demo-tweet-body">
+            <div className="demo-tweet-head">
+              <span className="demo-tweet-name">{displayName}</span>
+              <span className="demo-tweet-handle">@{example.author}</span>
+              {thread.length > 1 && (
+                <span className="demo-tweet-index">{i + 1}/{thread.length}</span>
+              )}
+            </div>
+            <p className="demo-tweet-text">{text}</p>
+            <div className="demo-tweet-meta">
+              <span className={`demo-char-count${text.length > 280 ? ' is-over' : ''}`}>
+                {text.length}/280
+              </span>
+            </div>
+          </div>
+        </article>
+      ))}
+    </div>
+  );
+}
+
+export default function Demo() {
+  const [exampleId, setExampleId] = useState(DEMO_EXAMPLES[0].id);
+  const [personaKey, setPersonaKey] = useState(PERSONA_KEYS[0]);
+
+  const example = useMemo(
+    () => DEMO_EXAMPLES.find((e) => e.id === exampleId),
+    [exampleId],
+  );
+  const persona = example.personas[personaKey];
+  const prompt = useMemo(() => example.promptTemplate(persona), [example, persona]);
+
+  return (
+    <div className="demo">
+      <section className="demo-intro">
+        <span className="demo-eyebrow">Live demo · no login · no backend</span>
+        <h1>See the gitlogs AI pipeline, end to end.</h1>
+        <p>
+          This is a live, no-login demo replaying real fixtures through the gitlogs AI pipeline.
+          Pick a commit, watch its git diff become an interpolated Gemini prompt, and read the
+          changelog post it generates. Switch persona to regenerate the same diff in a different
+          voice. Everything below runs entirely in your browser.
+        </p>
+        <Link to="/" className="demo-back">&larr; Back to home</Link>
+      </section>
+
+      <div className="demo-toolbar">
+        <div className="demo-selector" role="tablist" aria-label="Example commits">
+          {DEMO_EXAMPLES.map((e) => (
+            <button
+              key={e.id}
+              role="tab"
+              aria-selected={e.id === exampleId}
+              className={`demo-tab${e.id === exampleId ? ' is-active' : ''}`}
+              onClick={() => setExampleId(e.id)}
+            >
+              <span className="demo-tab-repo">{e.repoFullName}</span>
+              <span className="demo-tab-sha">{e.commit.sha}</span>
+            </button>
+          ))}
+        </div>
+
+        <div className="demo-personas" role="radiogroup" aria-label="Persona">
+          <span className="demo-personas-label">Persona</span>
+          {PERSONA_KEYS.map((key) => (
+            <button
+              key={key}
+              role="radio"
+              aria-checked={key === personaKey}
+              className={`demo-persona-btn${key === personaKey ? ' is-active' : ''}`}
+              onClick={() => setPersonaKey(key)}
+            >
+              {example.personas[key].label}
+            </button>
+          ))}
+        </div>
+      </div>
+
+      <div className="demo-pipeline">
+        {/* Stage 1: commit + diff */}
+        <section className="demo-stage" aria-labelledby="stage-input">
+          <header className="demo-stage-head">
+            <span className="demo-stage-num">01</span>
+            <h2 id="stage-input">Commit &amp; diff</h2>
+          </header>
+          <div className="demo-card demo-commit">
+            <div className="demo-commit-repo">{example.repoFullName}</div>
+            <div className="demo-commit-msg">{example.commit.message}</div>
+            <div className="demo-commit-refs">
+              <span className="demo-chip">{example.commit.branch}</span>
+              <span className="demo-chip demo-chip-sha">{example.commit.sha}</span>
+              <span className="demo-chip">@{example.author}</span>
+            </div>
+            <DiffView diff={example.diff} />
+          </div>
+        </section>
+
+        {/* Stage 2: prompt */}
+        <section className="demo-stage" aria-labelledby="stage-prompt">
+          <header className="demo-stage-head">
+            <span className="demo-stage-num">02</span>
+            <h2 id="stage-prompt">Gemini prompt</h2>
+          </header>
+          <div className="demo-card demo-prompt">
+            <div className="demo-prompt-label">
+              Persona: <strong>{persona.label}</strong>
+            </div>
+            <pre className="demo-prompt-body"><code>{prompt}</code></pre>
+          </div>
+        </section>
+
+        {/* Stage 3: output */}
+        <section className="demo-stage" aria-labelledby="stage-output">
+          <header className="demo-stage-head">
+            <span className="demo-stage-num">03</span>
+            <h2 id="stage-output">Generated post</h2>
+          </header>
+          <div className="demo-card demo-output">
+            <TweetCard example={example} thread={persona.thread} />
+          </div>
+        </section>
+      </div>
+    </div>
+  );
+}

"C:\\Users\\Aayushman\\AppData\\Local\\Microsoft\\WindowsApps\\pwsh.exe" -Command 'Get-Content -Path C:/Users/Aayushman/.codex/plugins/cache/claude-plugins-official/superpowers/5.1.0/skills/using-superpowers/SKILL.md -TotalCount 120' in C:\Repo\gitlogs
 succeeded in 536ms:
---
name: using-superpowers
description: Use when starting any conversation - establishes how to find and use skills, requiring Skill tool invocation before ANY response including clarifying questions
---

<SUBAGENT-STOP>
If you were dispatched as a subagent to execute a specific task, skip this skill.
</SUBAGENT-STOP>

<EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>
If you think there is even a 1% chance a skill might apply to what you are doing, you ABSOLUTELY MUST invoke the skill.

IF A SKILL APPLIES TO YOUR TASK, YOU DO NOT HAVE A CHOICE. YOU MUST USE IT.

This is not negotiable. This is not optional. You cannot rationalize your way out of this.
</EXTREMELY-IMPORTANT>

## Instruction Priority

Superpowers skills override default system prompt behavior, but **user instructions always take precedence**:

1. **User's explicit instructions** (CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, AGENTS.md, direct requests) — highest priority
2. **Superpowers skills** — override default system behavior where they conflict
3. **Default system prompt** — lowest priority

If CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, or AGENTS.md says "don't use TDD" and a skill says "always use TDD," follow the user's instructions. The user is in control.

## How to Access Skills

**In Claude Code:** Use the `Skill` tool. When you invoke a skill, its content is loaded and presented to you—follow it directly. Never use the Read tool on skill files.

**In Copilot CLI:** Use the `skill` tool. Skills are auto-discovered from installed plugins. The `skill` tool works the same as Claude Code's `Skill` tool.

**In Gemini CLI:** Skills activate via the `activate_skill` tool. Gemini loads skill metadata at session start and activates the full content on demand.

**In other environments:** Check your platform's documentation for how skills are loaded.

## Platform Adaptation

Skills use Claude Code tool names. Non-CC platforms: see `references/copilot-tools.md` (Copilot CLI), `references/codex-tools.md` (Codex) for tool equivalents. Gemini CLI users get the tool mapping loaded automatically via GEMINI.md.

# Using Skills

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action.** Even a 1% chance a skill might apply means that you should invoke the skill to check. If an invoked skill turns out to be wrong for the situation, you don't need to use it.

```dot
digraph skill_flow {
    "User message received" [shape=doublecircle];
    "About to EnterPlanMode?" [shape=doublecircle];
    "Already brainstormed?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" [shape=box];
    "Might any skill apply?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke Skill tool" [shape=box];
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" [shape=box];
    "Has checklist?" [shape=diamond];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [shape=box];
    "Follow skill exactly" [shape=box];
    "Respond (including clarifications)" [shape=doublecircle];

    "About to EnterPlanMode?" -> "Already brainstormed?";
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Invoke brainstorming skill" [label="no"];
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Might any skill apply?" [label="yes"];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" -> "Might any skill apply?";

    "User message received" -> "Might any skill apply?";
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Invoke Skill tool" [label="yes, even 1%"];
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Respond (including clarifications)" [label="definitely not"];
    "Invoke Skill tool" -> "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'";
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" -> "Has checklist?";
    "Has checklist?" -> "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [label="yes"];
    "Has checklist?" -> "Follow skill exactly" [label="no"];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" -> "Follow skill exactly";
}
```

## Red Flags

These thoughts mean STOP—you're rationalizing:

| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept ≠ using the skill. Invoke it. |

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills could apply, use this order:

1. **Process skills first** (brainstorming, debugging) - these determine HOW to approach the task
2. **Implementation skills second** (frontend-design, mcp-builder) - these guide execution

"Let's build X" → brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
"Fix this bug" → debugging first, then domain-specific skills.

## Skill Types

**Rigid** (TDD, debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.

**Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.

The skill itself tells you which.

## User Instructions

Instructions say WHAT, not HOW. "Add X" or "Fix Y" doesn't mean skip workflows.

frontend/src/utils/api.js:3:// Get backend URL from build-time env (VITE_API_BASE).
frontend/src/utils/api.js:4:// In dev, default to the local backend. In a PRODUCTION build, refuse to guess:
frontend/src/utils/api.js:5:// a prod bundle silently pointing at localhost would ship a broken app, so fail
frontend/src/utils/api.js:6:// loudly instead of falling back (per the project's no-silent-fallback rule).
frontend/src/utils/api.js:7:export function getBackendUrl() {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:8:  const base = import.meta.env.VITE_API_BASE;
frontend/src/utils/api.js:9:  if (base) return base;
frontend/src/utils/api.js:10:  if (import.meta.env.PROD) {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:11:    throw new Error(
frontend/src/utils/api.js:12:      'VITE_API_BASE is not set. Set it at build time for production builds ' +
frontend/src/utils/api.js:13:        '(e.g. VITE_API_BASE=https://api.example.com pnpm build).'
frontend/src/utils/api.js:14:    );
frontend/src/utils/api.js:15:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:16:  return 'http://localhost:3000';
frontend/src/utils/api.js:17:}

frontend/src/utils/api.js:31:export async function adminApiCall(endpoint, options = {}) {

frontend/src/utils/api.js:33:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:34:  const headers = {

frontend/src/utils/api.js:41:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:42:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:43:  const response = await fetch(`${API_BASE}${endpoint}`, {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:44:    ...options,
frontend/src/utils/api.js:45:    headers
frontend/src/utils/api.js:46:  });
frontend/src/utils/api.js:47:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:48:  // Check if response is JSON before parsing
frontend/src/utils/api.js:49:  const contentType = response.headers.get('content-type');
frontend/src/utils/api.js:50:  const isJson = contentType && contentType.includes('application/json');
frontend/src/utils/api.js:51:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:52:  let data;
frontend/src/utils/api.js:53:  if (isJson) {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:54:    try {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:55:      data = await response.json();
frontend/src/utils/api.js:56:    } catch (parseError) {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:57:      throw new Error(`Failed to parse JSON response: ${response.status} ${response.statusText}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:58:    }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:59:  } else {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:60:    // If not JSON, read as text for error message
frontend/src/utils/api.js:61:    const text = await response.text();
frontend/src/utils/api.js:62:    throw new Error(`Server returned non-JSON response (${response.status} ${response.statusText}): ${text.substring(0, 100)}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:63:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:64:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:65:  if (!response.ok) {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:66:    throw new Error(data.error || data.message || `HTTP ${response.status}: ${response.statusText}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:67:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:68:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:69:  return data;
frontend/src/utils/api.js:70:}

frontend/src/utils/api.js:94:      throw new Error(`Failed to parse JSON response: ${response.status} ${response.statusText}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:95:    }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:96:  } else {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:97:    // If not JSON, read as text for error message
frontend/src/utils/api.js:98:    const text = await response.text();
frontend/src/utils/api.js:99:    throw new Error(`Server returned non-JSON response (${response.status} ${response.statusText}): ${text.substring(0, 100)}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:100:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:101:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:102:  if (!response.ok) {
frontend/src/utils/api.js:103:    throw new Error(data.error || data.message || `HTTP ${response.status}: ${response.statusText}`);
frontend/src/utils/api.js:104:  }
frontend/src/utils/api.js:105:  
frontend/src/utils/api.js:106:  return data;
frontend/src/utils/api.js:107:}
frontend/src/utils/api.js:108:

README.md:1:# GitLogs
README.md:2:
README.md:3:**Turn `git push` into a published changelog tweet.** Sign in with GitHub, link your X account, enable a repo — every push then fires a webhook, Gemini summarizes the real diff, and a changelog post lands on your own X timeline. No manual tweeting, no abandoned changelog.
README.md:4:
README.md:5:[![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-c8693d?style=flat)](LICENSE)
README.md:6:[![Demo: /demo (no login)](https://img.shields.io/badge/Demo-%2Fdemo%20(no%20login)-3fb950?style=flat)](#see-it-in-30-seconds)
README.md:7:[![Node](https://img.shields.io/badge/Node-%3E%3D18-1f6feb?style=flat)](package.json)
README.md:8:
README.md:9:---
README.md:10:
README.md:11:## Why
README.md:12:
README.md:13:Developers ship constantly but rarely tell anyone. Manual tweeting kills momentum; abandoned changelogs kill discoverability. GitLogs closes the loop — you push code, the world hears about it. Gemini turns raw diffs into reader-friendly prose grounded in what actually changed, and webhooks fire the whole thing on every commit.
README.md:14:
README.md:15:## See it in 30 seconds
README.md:16:
README.md:17:There's a **keyless `/demo` route** — no GitHub, no X, no API keys. It replays bundled commit fixtures through the real pipeline shape entirely client-side: a commit + diff become an interpolated Gemini prompt, which becomes a generated changelog post. A persona toggle (Professional / Hype / Deadpan Technical) re-renders the prompt and output so you can see the prompt engineering, not just the result.
README.md:18:
README.md:19:Run it locally:
README.md:20:
README.md:21:```bash
README.md:22:pnpm setup && pnpm dev:all
README.md:23:# then open http://localhost:5173/demo
README.md:24:```
README.md:25:
README.md:26:A hosted demo link is pending deployment — see the **Demo** badge above once it's live.
README.md:27:
README.md:28:### Example output
README.md:29:
README.md:30:A real generated post from the demo fixtures, for commit `a1b2c3d` on `octo-dev/payments-api` (`feat: idempotency keys on POST /charges`), in the **Professional** persona:
README.md:31:
README.md:32:> shipped: idempotency keys on POST /charges. retries now return the original charge instead of creating a duplicate. one required header, zero double-charges. (a1b2c3d)
README.md:33:
README.md:34:The same diff in **Deadpan Technical**:
README.md:35:
README.md:36:> POST /charges: require Idempotency-Key header (400 if missing). lookup by key first, return existing charge 200 if found, else create with key. backed by a partial unique index where key is not null. (a1b2c3d)
README.md:37:
README.md:38:The prompt feeds Gemini the actual diff as ground truth and instructs it to describe only what changed — no hallucinated features.
README.md:39:
README.md:40:## How it works
README.md:41:
README.md:42:Every push hits `POST /webhook/github`. The backend verifies the GitHub HMAC signature (failing **closed** if no secret is configured — see [security](#configuration)), resolves which user owns the repo, and runs a two-stage AI pipeline per non-merge commit: Stage 1 fetches the real diff from the GitHub REST API and asks Gemini for a factual summary; Stage 2 feeds that grounded summary into the user's prompt template and posts the result to their own X account. Stage 2 runs through a rate-limited, retrying, restart-survivable queue backed by SQLite.
README.md:43:
README.md:44:```mermaid
README.md:45:sequenceDiagram
README.md:46:    autonumber
README.md:47:    participant GH as GitHub
README.md:48:    participant WH as webhookHandler
README.md:49:    participant DA as diffAnalyzer
README.md:50:    participant GEM as geminiClient
README.md:51:    participant Q as queueService
README.md:52:    participant DB as SQLite (sql.js)
README.md:53:    participant TW as twitterClient / X
README.md:54:
README.md:55:    GH->>WH: POST push (raw body + x-hub-signature-256)
README.md:56:    WH->>WH: HMAC-SHA256 verify (timingSafeEqual; fail CLOSED if no secret)
README.md:57:    alt invalid or no secret
README.md:58:        WH-->>GH: 401 reject
README.md:59:    else valid
README.md:60:        WH->>DB: resolve repo -> user -> X auth
README.md:61:        loop each non-merge commit
README.md:62:            WH->>DA: fetchCommitDiff(repo, sha)
README.md:63:            DA-->>WH: diff + files + stats
README.md:64:            WH->>GEM: analyzeDiff(diff) — Stage 1 (factual summary)
README.md:65:            WH->>GEM: generateChangelog(commit, diffSummary) — Stage 2
README.md:66:            GEM->>Q: enqueue task (persisted, rate-limited)
README.md:67:            Q->>DB: saveQueueItem(pending)
README.md:68:            Q->>GEM: run template + diffSummary through Gemini (retry w/ backoff)
README.md:69:            GEM-->>WH: changelog text
README.md:70:            WH->>TW: postTweet(text, optional quote)
README.md:71:            TW-->>WH: tweet id
README.md:72:            WH->>DB: saveTweetId(repo, sha, tweetId)
README.md:73:        end
README.md:74:        WH-->>GH: 200 { processed, total }
README.md:75:    end
README.md:76:```
README.md:77:
README.md:78:For the full sequence, OAuth flows, data model, and documented failure modes, see [`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`](docs/ARCHITECTURE.md).
README.md:79:
README.md:80:## Quick start
README.md:81:
README.md:82:Requires **Node >= 18** and **pnpm**. Windows, macOS, and Linux are all supported (the codebase is developed on Windows). Lockfiles are committed (root + `frontend/`) for reproducible installs.
README.md:83:
README.md:84:```bash
README.md:85:git clone https://github.com/aayushman-singh/git-twitter-bot.git gitlogs
README.md:86:cd gitlogs
README.md:87:
README.md:88:pnpm setup            # install backend + frontend deps
README.md:89:cp .env.example .env  # fill in your keys (see Configuration)
README.md:90:pnpm seed             # populate a demo SQLite db with fixtures
README.md:91:pnpm dev:all          # backend (nodemon) + Vite dev server together
README.md:92:```
README.md:93:
README.md:94:Then open the dashboard at `http://localhost:5173` or the keyless demo at `http://localhost:5173/demo`.
README.md:95:
README.md:96:```bash
README.md:97:pnpm test             # run the Vitest backend suite
README.md:98:pnpm build            # build the SPA to frontend/dist
README.md:99:```
README.md:100:
README.md:101:## Stack
README.md:102:
README.md:103:| Layer | Tech |
README.md:104:| --- | --- |
README.md:105:| Frontend | React 18 · Vite 5 · PrimeReact · React Router |
README.md:106:| Backend | Node.js · Express 4 |
README.md:107:| Datastore | SQLite via [sql.js](https://sql.js.org) (WASM, single-file) |
README.md:108:| AI | Google Gemini — two-stage diff analysis + changelog generation |
README.md:109:| Auth | GitHub OAuth2 (login + webhook control) · X OAuth 2.0 with PKCE (posting) |
README.md:110:
README.md:111:The backend is a single Express process that also serves the built SPA from `frontend/dist` in production.
README.md:112:
README.md:113:## Configuration
README.md:114:
README.md:115:Copy `.env.example` to `.env` and fill in real values — every value in the example is a placeholder. The key groups:
README.md:116:
README.md:117:- **GitHub OAuth** — `GITHUB_CLIENT_ID`, `GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET` (create an OAuth app at github.com/settings/developers).
README.md:118:- **Webhook secret** — `WEBHOOK_SECRET`. **Do not skip this.** Signature verification fails *closed*: with no secret configured, every incoming webhook is rejected rather than trusted. Generate one with `openssl rand -hex 20`.
README.md:119:- **X OAuth 2.0** — `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` (required), `OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` (optional, enables confidential-client mode), `OAUTH_CALLBACK_URL`.
README.md:120:- **Gemini** — `GEMINI_API_KEY`, `GEMINI_MODEL` (default in the example is `gemini-2.5-flash`). Get a key at aistudio.google.com/app/apikey.
README.md:121:- **Server** — `PORT`, `FRONTEND_URL`, `API_BASE_URL`, `DATABASE_PATH`, `ADMIN_API_KEY` (gates the `/api/*` admin routes), plus optional queue/rate-limit tuning (`QUEUE_MAX_RPM`, `QUEUE_MAX_RETRIES`, ...).
README.md:122:
README.md:123:## API
README.md:124:
README.md:125:| Method | Path | Purpose |
README.md:126:| --- | --- | --- |
README.md:127:| `GET` | `/auth/github` | Start GitHub OAuth login |
README.md:128:| `GET` | `/auth/github/callback` | GitHub OAuth callback |
README.md:129:| `GET` | `/auth/x` | Start X OAuth 2.0 PKCE flow (requires GitHub login) |
README.md:130:| `GET` | `/auth/x/callback` | X OAuth callback |
README.md:131:| `POST` | `/auth/logout` | Clear session + stored token |
README.md:132:| `POST` | `/webhook/github` | GitHub push webhook receiver (HMAC-verified) |
README.md:133:| `GET` | `/api/me` | Current user + X connection status |
README.md:134:| `GET` | `/api/me/repos` | User repositories with enabled/OG status |
README.md:135:| `POST` | `/api/me/repos/enable` | Enable a repo (creates the webhook) |
README.md:136:| `POST` | `/api/me/repos/disable` | Disable a repo (removes the webhook) |
README.md:137:| `GET` | `/api/me/templates` | List the user's prompt templates |
README.md:138:| `GET` | `/api/health` | Health check (queue + feature flags) |
README.md:139:| `GET` | `/api/stats` | Queue + system stats (admin, API-key gated) |
README.md:140:
README.md:141:## Testing
README.md:142:
README.md:143:```bash
README.md:144:pnpm test        # one-shot Vitest run
README.md:145:pnpm test:watch  # watch mode
README.md:146:```
README.md:147:
README.md:148:The backend suite (`tests/`) covers a **webhook end-to-end test** (`webhook.e2e.test.js`) — driving a signed push payload through the wired Express app via supertest — and the **queue mechanics** (`queue.test.js`): rate limiting, retry/backoff, and restart persistence.
README.md:149:
README.md:150:## Architecture
README.md:151:
README.md:152:A single Express process serves the React SPA, terminates both OAuth flows, verifies and processes webhooks, and persists everything to a single-file sql.js database. Full component map, sequence diagrams, ER model, and a candid list of known weaknesses live in [`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`](docs/ARCHITECTURE.md).
README.md:153:
README.md:154:## Contributing
README.md:155:
README.md:156:1. Fork the repo and create a branch off `main` (`feat/...`, `fix/...`).
README.md:157:2. Make atomic commits with [Conventional Commit](https://www.conventionalcommits.org) messages (`feat:`, `fix:`, `docs:`, ...).
README.md:158:3. Make sure `pnpm test` passes.
README.md:159:4. Open a pull request describing the change and the user-facing impact.

README.md:165:## License
README.md:166:

RUNBOOK.md:1:# RUNBOOK — gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:2:
RUNBOOK.md:3:Operational guide for the **keyed production path** (the full product: GitHub
RUNBOOK.md:4:OAuth, X OAuth, Gemini, live posting) and the **keyless demo deploy** (the
RUNBOOK.md:5:public `/demo` showcase). Every secret below is templated — fill in your own.
RUNBOOK.md:6:
RUNBOOK.md:7:---
RUNBOOK.md:8:
RUNBOOK.md:9:## 0. Secret rotation (do this FIRST)
RUNBOOK.md:10:
RUNBOOK.md:11:The repository's history is clean of real secrets (`.env` was never committed;
RUNBOOK.md:12:`.env.example` was scrubbed of the partial OAuth credentials it once held). But
RUNBOOK.md:13:the live credentials that previously sat in a local `.env` should be treated as
RUNBOOK.md:14:compromised and **rotated before any production deploy**:
RUNBOOK.md:15:
RUNBOOK.md:16:| Credential | Where to rotate |
RUNBOOK.md:17:| --- | --- |
RUNBOOK.md:18:| GitHub OAuth client secret | github.com/settings/developers → your OAuth app → "Generate a new client secret" |
RUNBOOK.md:19:| X / Twitter OAuth2 client secret | developer.twitter.com → your app → Keys and tokens → regenerate |
RUNBOOK.md:20:| X / Twitter API key/secret + access token/secret + bearer | same X app → regenerate all |
RUNBOOK.md:21:| Gemini API key | aistudio.google.com/app/apikey → revoke + create new |
RUNBOOK.md:22:| Cloudflare API token | dash.cloudflare.com → My Profile → API Tokens → roll |
RUNBOOK.md:23:| `WEBHOOK_SECRET` | regenerate: `openssl rand -hex 20` (then update each repo's webhook) |
RUNBOOK.md:24:| `ADMIN_API_KEY` | regenerate: `openssl rand -hex 32` |
RUNBOOK.md:25:
RUNBOOK.md:26:After rotating, put the new values **only** in the server's `.env` (git-ignored)
RUNBOOK.md:27:and in your deploy provider's secret store. Never commit them.
RUNBOOK.md:28:
RUNBOOK.md:29:---
RUNBOOK.md:30:
RUNBOOK.md:31:## 1. Provision the integrations (one-time)
RUNBOOK.md:32:
RUNBOOK.md:33:1. **GitHub OAuth app** — github.com/settings/developers → New OAuth App.
RUNBOOK.md:34:   - Homepage: `https://<your-frontend-domain>`
RUNBOOK.md:35:   - Callback: `https://<your-api-domain>/auth/github/callback`
RUNBOOK.md:36:   - Copy `GITHUB_CLIENT_ID` / `GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET`.
RUNBOOK.md:37:2. **X (Twitter) app** — developer.twitter.com → Project → App with **OAuth 2.0**.
RUNBOOK.md:38:   - Type: Web App / Confidential client.
RUNBOOK.md:39:   - Callback: `https://<your-api-domain>/auth/x/callback`
RUNBOOK.md:40:   - Scopes: `tweet.read tweet.write users.read offline.access`.
RUNBOOK.md:41:   - Copy `OAUTH_CLIENT_ID` / `OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET` (+ the API keys/tokens).
RUNBOOK.md:42:3. **Gemini** — aistudio.google.com/app/apikey → `GEMINI_API_KEY`.
RUNBOOK.md:43:
RUNBOOK.md:44:---
RUNBOOK.md:45:
RUNBOOK.md:46:## 2. Configure `.env`
RUNBOOK.md:47:
RUNBOOK.md:48:```bash
RUNBOOK.md:49:cp .env.example .env
RUNBOOK.md:50:```
RUNBOOK.md:51:
RUNBOOK.md:52:Fill in (see `.env.example` for the full annotated list):
RUNBOOK.md:53:
RUNBOOK.md:54:```ini
RUNBOOK.md:55:NODE_ENV=production
RUNBOOK.md:56:PORT=3000
RUNBOOK.md:57:FRONTEND_URL=https://<your-frontend-domain>
RUNBOOK.md:58:API_BASE_URL=https://<your-api-domain>
RUNBOOK.md:59:
RUNBOOK.md:60:GITHUB_CLIENT_ID=<rotated>
RUNBOOK.md:61:GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET=<rotated>
RUNBOOK.md:62:
RUNBOOK.md:63:OAUTH_CLIENT_ID=<rotated>          # X OAuth2 client id
RUNBOOK.md:64:OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET=<rotated>
RUNBOOK.md:65:OAUTH_CALLBACK_URL=https://<your-api-domain>/auth/x/callback
RUNBOOK.md:66:
RUNBOOK.md:67:GEMINI_API_KEY=<rotated>
RUNBOOK.md:68:GEMINI_MODEL=gemini-2.5-flash
RUNBOOK.md:69:
RUNBOOK.md:70:WEBHOOK_SECRET=<openssl rand -hex 20>   # REQUIRED — HMAC fails CLOSED without it
RUNBOOK.md:71:ADMIN_API_KEY=<openssl rand -hex 32>
RUNBOOK.md:72:DATABASE_PATH=./tweets.db
RUNBOOK.md:73:ALLOWED_REPOS=                          # empty = accept all enabled repos
RUNBOOK.md:74:```
RUNBOOK.md:75:
RUNBOOK.md:76:> **Fail-closed note:** with no `WEBHOOK_SECRET`, every incoming webhook is
RUNBOOK.md:77:> rejected (401). This is intentional — a missing secret is a misconfiguration,
RUNBOOK.md:78:> not a reason to trust unsigned payloads.
RUNBOOK.md:79:
RUNBOOK.md:80:---
RUNBOOK.md:81:
RUNBOOK.md:82:## 3. One-command server bring-up (EC2 / any Node host)
RUNBOOK.md:83:
RUNBOOK.md:84:```bash
RUNBOOK.md:85:git clone https://github.com/aayushman-singh/git-twitter-bot.git ~/gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:86:cd ~/gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:87:corepack enable && corepack prepare pnpm@latest --activate   # if pnpm absent
RUNBOOK.md:88:pnpm install --frozen-lockfile
RUNBOOK.md:89:pnpm --dir frontend install --frozen-lockfile
RUNBOOK.md:90:VITE_API_BASE=https://<your-api-domain> pnpm --dir frontend run build
RUNBOOK.md:91:# (.env already in place from step 2)
RUNBOOK.md:92:node src/server.js     # or via systemd, below
RUNBOOK.md:93:```
RUNBOOK.md:94:
RUNBOOK.md:95:The backend serves the built SPA from `frontend/dist` and exposes the API +
RUNBOOK.md:96:`/webhook/github` on `PORT`.
RUNBOOK.md:97:
RUNBOOK.md:98:### systemd unit (template)
RUNBOOK.md:99:
RUNBOOK.md:100:`/etc/systemd/system/gitlogs.service`:
RUNBOOK.md:101:
RUNBOOK.md:102:```ini
RUNBOOK.md:103:[Unit]
RUNBOOK.md:104:Description=gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:105:After=network.target
RUNBOOK.md:106:
RUNBOOK.md:107:[Service]
RUNBOOK.md:108:Type=simple
RUNBOOK.md:109:User=<deploy-user>
RUNBOOK.md:110:WorkingDirectory=/home/<deploy-user>/gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:111:EnvironmentFile=/home/<deploy-user>/gitlogs/.env
RUNBOOK.md:112:ExecStart=/usr/bin/node src/server.js
RUNBOOK.md:113:Restart=on-failure
RUNBOOK.md:114:RestartSec=5
RUNBOOK.md:115:
RUNBOOK.md:116:[Install]
RUNBOOK.md:117:WantedBy=multi-user.target
RUNBOOK.md:118:```
RUNBOOK.md:119:
RUNBOOK.md:120:```bash
RUNBOOK.md:121:sudo systemctl daemon-reload
RUNBOOK.md:122:sudo systemctl enable --now gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:123:sudo systemctl status gitlogs
RUNBOOK.md:124:```
RUNBOOK.md:125:
RUNBOOK.md:126:---
RUNBOOK.md:127:
RUNBOOK.md:128:## 4. Continuous deploy (GitHub Actions → EC2)
RUNBOOK.md:129:
RUNBOOK.md:130:`.github/workflows/deploy-ec2.yml` SSHes in on push to `main`, pulls, installs
RUNBOOK.md:131:from the frozen lockfiles, **builds the frontend**, and restarts the service.
RUNBOOK.md:132:
RUNBOOK.md:133:Required repo **Actions secrets** (Settings → Secrets and variables → Actions):
RUNBOOK.md:134:
RUNBOOK.md:135:| Secret | Value |
RUNBOOK.md:136:| --- | --- |
RUNBOOK.md:137:| `EC2_HOST` | server hostname / IP |
RUNBOOK.md:138:| `EC2_USER` | ssh user (the systemd `User=`) |
RUNBOOK.md:139:| `EC2_SSH_KEY` | private key authorized on the host |
RUNBOOK.md:140:| `EC2_PORT` | ssh port (optional, defaults to 22) |
RUNBOOK.md:141:
RUNBOOK.md:142:Also set `VITE_API_BASE` in the deploy environment (or edit the workflow's
RUNBOOK.md:143:default) so the SPA is built against the right API origin.
RUNBOOK.md:144:
RUNBOOK.md:145:> **Known tradeoff (codex review):** the workflow currently builds on the prod
RUNBOOK.md:146:> host. For a hardened setup, build the SPA artifact in CI and ship only
RUNBOOK.md:147:> `frontend/dist` to the host, so prod carries no dev/build toolchain. Tracked
RUNBOOK.md:148:> as a follow-up; the current approach is fine for a single small instance.
RUNBOOK.md:149:
RUNBOOK.md:150:---
RUNBOOK.md:151:
RUNBOOK.md:152:## 5. DNS
RUNBOOK.md:153:
RUNBOOK.md:154:The historical hosts `gitlogs.aayushman.dev` / `api-gitlogs.aayushman.dev` are
RUNBOOK.md:155:NXDOMAIN. Point:
RUNBOOK.md:156:
RUNBOOK.md:157:- `<your-frontend-domain>` → the host (or the static SPA deploy).
RUNBOOK.md:158:- `<your-api-domain>` → the EC2 instance running the backend.
RUNBOOK.md:159:
RUNBOOK.md:160:Update the GitHub + X OAuth callback URLs and `.env` to match.
RUNBOOK.md:161:
RUNBOOK.md:162:---
RUNBOOK.md:163:
RUNBOOK.md:164:## 6. Keyless demo deploy (Vercel / Cloudflare Pages)
RUNBOOK.md:165:
RUNBOOK.md:166:The `/demo` route is fully client-side (no backend, no keys) — ideal for a
RUNBOOK.md:167:static host. Because `frontend/src/utils/api.js` fails loudly in production
RUNBOOK.md:168:builds when `VITE_API_BASE` is unset, pass a value at build time even though the
RUNBOOK.md:169:demo never calls it.
RUNBOOK.md:170:
RUNBOOK.md:171:**Vercel** (root directory = `frontend/`):
RUNBOOK.md:172:- Build command: `pnpm build`
RUNBOOK.md:173:- Output dir: `dist`
RUNBOOK.md:174:- Env: `VITE_API_BASE = https://<your-api-domain>` (or any placeholder)
RUNBOOK.md:175:- `frontend/vercel.json` already provides the SPA rewrite so `/demo` deep-links.
RUNBOOK.md:176:
RUNBOOK.md:177:```bash
RUNBOOK.md:178:# from the frontend/ directory, with the Vercel CLI authenticated:
RUNBOOK.md:179:VITE_API_BASE=https://gitlogs.example pnpm build
RUNBOOK.md:180:npx vercel deploy --prebuilt --prod   # or `npx vercel` and follow prompts
RUNBOOK.md:181:```
RUNBOOK.md:182:
RUNBOOK.md:183:**Cloudflare Pages**:
RUNBOOK.md:184:- Build command: `pnpm build`  · Output: `frontend/dist`  · Root: `frontend`
RUNBOOK.md:185:- Or direct upload: `npx wrangler pages deploy frontend/dist`
RUNBOOK.md:186:
RUNBOOK.md:187:After deploying, update the **Demo** badge/link in `README.md` with the live URL.
RUNBOOK.md:188:
RUNBOOK.md:189:---
RUNBOOK.md:190:
RUNBOOK.md:191:## 7. Verify a deploy
RUNBOOK.md:192:
RUNBOOK.md:193:```bash
RUNBOOK.md:194:curl -s https://<your-api-domain>/api/health        # → 200 JSON
RUNBOOK.md:195:# Push a commit to an enabled repo, then check the X account + logs:
RUNBOOK.md:196:sudo journalctl -u gitlogs -f
RUNBOOK.md:197:```
RUNBOOK.md:198:
RUNBOOK.md:199:A correctly working pipeline logs: signature verified → repo/user resolved →
RUNBOOK.md:200:diff fetched → Stage 1/2 Gemini → queued → posted tweet id → persisted.

.env.example:8:# Public URL of the frontend (used for CORS + OAuth redirects)

docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:5:GitLogs turns a `git push` into a published changelog tweet. A developer signs in with GitHub, picks a repository, and GitLogs installs a `push` webhook on it. From then on, every push fires `POST /webhook/github`; the backend verifies the GitHub HMAC signature, resolves which user owns the repo, and for each non-merge commit runs a two-stage AI pipeline — Stage 1 fetches the real commit diff from the GitHub REST API and asks Gemini to summarize it factually; Stage 2 feeds that grounded summary into the user's prompt template (AI-expanded only if the template contains `{{AI_TEXT}}`) to produce tweet text. The text is posted to the developer's own X account via OAuth 2.0 PKCE, optionally quoting a pinned "OG" tweet, and the resulting tweet ID is persisted. The Stage-2 changelog generation runs through a rate-limited, retrying, restart-survivable queue backed by SQLite (sql.js); note that the Stage-1 diff analysis calls Gemini directly and is **not** queued (a known weakness — see Failure modes). The whole thing is a single Node/Express process serving a React/Vite SPA from `frontend/dist`.
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:15:| `server.js` | Express wiring: static SPA hosting, CORS, cookie parsing, **raw-body capture for the webhook** (`server.js:29-36`), GitHub + X OAuth routes, `/api/me/*` user routes, admin `/api/*` routes (API-key gated), the GitHub API proxy, graceful shutdown. Mounts the webhook at `server.js:832`. |
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:18:| `geminiClient.js` | Two-stage AI. `analyzeDiff` (Stage 1, `:115`) summarizes the diff. `generateChangelog` (Stage 2, `:317`) builds a serializable task and **enqueues it on the queue service**; the task runs the template through `templateEngine`, calls Gemini only if `{{AI_TEXT}}` is present, and injects the Stage-1 summary as anti-hallucination grounding. Initializes the model and registers task factories on load. |
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:19:| `queueService.js` | Singleton rate-limited work queue. Caps to `maxRequestsPerMinute`, retries up to `maxRetries` with jittered exponential backoff (longer floor for rate-limit errors), persists every item to `queue_items`, and restores pending/processing items on startup. Driven by a `setInterval` every `processingIntervalMs`. |
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:25:| `config/config.js` | Single env-config surface (server, github, twitter, gemini, queue, multiUser). |
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:29:React 18 + Vite 5 SPA under `frontend/`, built to `frontend/dist` and served by the backend via `express.static` in production (`server.js:18-21`, SPA fallback at `:1094`). Talks to the backend through `VITE_API_BASE`; auth state rides on the `httpOnly` `github_user_id` cookie.

docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:251:| `queue_items` | Durable mirror of the in-memory Gemini queue so work resumes after restart. | `queue_id` unique, `task_type`, `data_json`, `status`, `retry_count` |
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:257:- **HMAC fails OPEN when no secret is configured.** `verifyGitHubSignature` returns `true` (and only logs a warning) if neither a per-repo secret nor `WEBHOOK_SECRET` is set (`webhookHandler.js:32-35`). With no secret, anyone who can reach `/webhook/github` can forge a push payload and trigger tweets. **Always set `WEBHOOK_SECRET`** (and note that webhook *creation* via `createWebhook` already refuses to proceed without one — `server.js:438`). With a secret set, signatures are compared with `crypto.timingSafeEqual`.
docs/ARCHITECTURE.md:259:- **Queue retry behavior.** Gemini work runs through `queueService`: capped at `QUEUE_MAX_RPM` requests/minute, retried up to `QUEUE_MAX_RETRIES` times with jittered exponential backoff (`QUEUE_BASE_RETRY_DELAY × 2^n`, capped at `QUEUE_MAX_RETRY_DELAY`; rate-limit errors get a ≥30s floor). Items are persisted in `queue_items` and restored on startup (`processing` items are reset to `pending`). After max retries an item is marked `failed` and dropped. Note Stage-1 `analyzeDiff` is **not** queued — it calls Gemini directly — so it isn't rate-limit-protected the way Stage 2 is.

src/server.js:179:// CORS configuration - allow frontend domain
src/server.js:180:const allowedOrigins = [
src/server.js:181:  'https://gitlogs.aayushman.dev',
src/server.js:182:  'http://localhost:5173', // Vite dev server
src/server.js:183:  'http://localhost:3000',
src/server.js:184:  process.env.FRONTEND_URL,
src/server.js:185:  config.server.frontendUrl
src/server.js:186:].filter(Boolean); // Remove undefined values
src/server.js:187:
src/server.js:188:app.use(cors({
src/server.js:189:  origin: function (origin, callback) {
src/server.js:190:    // Allow requests with no origin (like mobile apps, curl, Postman)
src/server.js:191:    if (!origin) return callback(null, true);
src/server.js:192:    
src/server.js:193:    if (allowedOrigins.includes(origin)) {
src/server.js:194:      callback(null, true);
src/server.js:195:    } else {
src/server.js:196:      console.log('CORS blocked origin:', origin);
src/server.js:197:      callback(new Error('Not allowed by CORS'));
src/server.js:198:    }
src/server.js:199:  },
src/server.js:200:  credentials: true,
src/server.js:201:  methods: ['GET', 'POST', 'PUT', 'DELETE', 'OPTIONS'],
src/server.js:202:  allowedHeaders: ['Content-Type', 'Authorization', 'x-api-key']
src/server.js:203:}));

src/server.js:217:  githubStateStore.set(state, Date.now());
src/server.js:218:  
src/server.js:219:  // Clean up old states (older than 10 minutes)
src/server.js:220:  const tenMinutesAgo = Date.now() - 10 * 60 * 1000;
src/server.js:221:  for (const [key, timestamp] of githubStateStore.entries()) {
src/server.js:222:    if (timestamp < tenMinutesAgo) {
src/server.js:223:      githubStateStore.delete(key);
src/server.js:224:    }
src/server.js:225:  }
src/server.js:226:  
src/server.js:227:  const authUrl = githubAuth.getAuthUrl(state);
src/server.js:228:  res.redirect(authUrl);

src/server.js:231:// GitHub OAuth callback - exchanges code for tokens (including refresh token)
src/server.js:232:app.get('/auth/github/callback', async (req, res) => {
src/server.js:233:  const { code, state, error } = req.query;
src/server.js:234:  
src/server.js:235:  if (error) {
src/server.js:236:    console.error('❌ GitHub OAuth error:', error);
src/server.js:237:    return res.redirect(`${FRONTEND_URL}/dashboard?error=${encodeURIComponent(error)}`);
src/server.js:238:  }
src/server.js:239:  
src/server.js:240:  if (!code || !state) {
src/server.js:241:    return res.redirect(`${FRONTEND_URL}/dashboard?error=missing_code`);
src/server.js:242:  }
src/server.js:243:  
src/server.js:244:  // Verify state
src/server.js:245:  if (!githubStateStore.has(state)) {
src/server.js:246:    return res.redirect(`${FRONTEND_URL}/dashboard?error=invalid_state`);
src/server.js:247:  }
src/server.js:248:  githubStateStore.delete(state);
src/server.js:249:  
src/server.js:250:  try {
src/server.js:251:    // Exchange code for tokens (access + refresh)
src/server.js:252:    const tokens = await githubAuth.exchangeCodeForTokens(code);
src/server.js:253:    
src/server.js:254:    // Get user info
src/server.js:255:    const user = await githubAuth.getGitHubUser(tokens.accessToken);
src/server.js:256:    
src/server.js:257:    // Calculate expiration time (if provided by GitHub)
src/server.js:258:    // GitHub Apps: tokens expire in ~8 hours
src/server.js:259:    // Classic OAuth: tokens don't expire (expiresIn will be null)
src/server.js:260:    const expiresAt = tokens.expiresIn 
src/server.js:261:      ? new Date(Date.now() + tokens.expiresIn * 1000)
src/server.js:262:      : null;
src/server.js:263:    
src/server.js:264:    // Store tokens in database (persistent, survives server restarts)
src/server.js:265:    database.storeGithubToken(
src/server.js:266:      user.id.toString(),
src/server.js:267:      tokens.accessToken,
src/server.js:268:      user,
src/server.js:269:      expiresAt,
src/server.js:270:      tokens.refreshToken
src/server.js:271:    );
src/server.js:272:    
src/server.js:273:    // Create/update user in database
src/server.js:274:    database.upsertUser({
src/server.js:275:      userId: `github:${user.id}`,
src/server.js:276:      githubUsername: user.login,
src/server.js:277:      displayName: user.name || user.login,
src/server.js:278:      email: user.email
src/server.js:279:    });
src/server.js:280:    
src/server.js:281:    // Set cookie to identify the user (long-lived - 6 months to match refresh token)
src/server.js:282:    res.cookie('github_user_id', user.id, {
src/server.js:283:      httpOnly: true,
src/server.js:284:      secure: true,
src/server.js:285:      sameSite: 'none',
src/server.js:286:      maxAge: 180 * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000, // 180 days (6 months)
src/server.js:287:      domain: config.server.nodeEnv === 'production' ? '.aayushman.dev' : undefined
src/server.js:288:    });
src/server.js:289:    
src/server.js:290:    const tokenType = tokens.refreshToken ? 'with refresh token' : 'classic (no expiry)';
src/server.js:291:    console.log(`✅ GitHub user logged in: @${user.login} (${tokenType})`);
src/server.js:292:    res.redirect(`${FRONTEND_URL}/dashboard?auth=success`);
src/server.js:293:  } catch (err) {
src/server.js:294:    console.error('❌ GitHub OAuth callback error:', err);
src/server.js:295:    res.redirect(`${FRONTEND_URL}/dashboard?error=${encodeURIComponent(err.message)}`);
src/server.js:296:  }
src/server.js:297:});
src/server.js:298:

src/server.js:309:// Get current user (based on stored GitHub token)
src/server.js:310:app.get('/api/me', async (req, res) => {
src/server.js:311:  const githubUserId = getGithubUserIdFromCookie(req);
src/server.js:312:  if (!githubUserId) {
src/server.js:313:    return res.status(401).json({ error: 'Not authenticated', user: null });
src/server.js:314:  }
src/server.js:315:  
src/server.js:316:  const tokenData = database.getGithubToken(githubUserId);
src/server.js:317:  if (!tokenData) {
src/server.js:318:    return res.status(401).json({ 
src/server.js:319:      error: 'not_authenticated', 
src/server.js:320:      message: 'Please sign in with GitHub.',
src/server.js:321:      user: null 
src/server.js:322:    });
src/server.js:323:  }
src/server.js:324:  
src/server.js:325:  // Try to get a valid token (will auto-refresh if needed)
src/server.js:326:  const validToken = await githubAuth.getValidAccessToken(githubUserId);
src/server.js:327:  if (!validToken) {
src/server.js:328:    return res.status(401).json({ 
src/server.js:329:      error: 'token_expired', 
src/server.js:330:      message: 'Session expired. Please sign in again.',
src/server.js:331:      user: null 
src/server.js:332:    });
src/server.js:333:  }
src/server.js:334:  
src/server.js:335:  // Get fresh token data after potential refresh
src/server.js:336:  const freshTokenData = database.getGithubToken(githubUserId);
src/server.js:337:  
src/server.js:338:  // Get X/Twitter user info if connected (per-user X OAuth)
src/server.js:339:  const xOAuthUserId = database.getXOAuthUserId(githubUserId);
src/server.js:340:  let xUserInfo = null;
src/server.js:341:  const xConnected = database.isOAuthTokenValid(xOAuthUserId);
src/server.js:342:  
src/server.js:343:  if (xConnected) {
src/server.js:344:    try {
src/server.js:345:      const { getXUserInfo } = require('./twitterClient');
src/server.js:346:      xUserInfo = await getXUserInfo(xOAuthUserId);
src/server.js:347:    } catch (err) {
src/server.js:348:      console.error('Failed to get X user info:', err.message);
src/server.js:349:      // Continue without X user info
src/server.js:350:    }
src/server.js:351:  }
src/server.js:352:  
src/server.js:353:  res.json({ 
src/server.js:354:    user: freshTokenData.user, 
src/server.js:355:    xConnected: xConnected,
src/server.js:356:    tokenExpiresAt: freshTokenData.expiresAt,
src/server.js:357:    hasRefreshToken: !!freshTokenData.refreshToken,
src/server.js:358:    xUserInfo: xUserInfo
src/server.js:359:  });
src/server.js:360:});
src/server.js:361:

src/server.js:404:// Enable posting for a repo
src/server.js:405:app.post('/api/me/repos/enable', async (req, res) => {
src/server.js:406:  const githubUserId = getGithubUserIdFromCookie(req);
src/server.js:407:  
src/server.js:408:  if (!githubUserId) {
src/server.js:409:    return res.status(401).json({ error: 'Not authenticated' });
src/server.js:410:  }
src/server.js:411:  
src/server.js:412:  const { repoFullName } = req.body;
src/server.js:413:  
src/server.js:414:  if (!repoFullName) {
src/server.js:415:    return res.status(400).json({ error: 'repoFullName is required' });
src/server.js:416:  }
src/server.js:417:  
src/server.js:418:  try {
src/server.js:419:    // Verify user has access to this repo (auto-refreshes token)
src/server.js:420:    const repos = await githubAuth.getUserRepos(githubUserId);
src/server.js:421:    const repo = repos.find(r => r.full_name === repoFullName);
src/server.js:422:    
src/server.js:423:    if (!repo) {
src/server.js:424:      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'You do not have access to this repository' });
src/server.js:425:    }
src/server.js:426:    
src/server.js:427:    // Check if user has admin access (required for webhook creation)
src/server.js:428:    if (!repo.permissions?.admin) {
src/server.js:429:      return res.status(403).json({ 
src/server.js:430:        error: 'Admin access required to enable webhooks. You need push access to this repository.' 
src/server.js:431:      });
src/server.js:432:    }
src/server.js:433:    
src/server.js:434:    // Create webhook automatically (uses auto-refresh)
src/server.js:435:    const webhookUrl = `${process.env.API_BASE_URL || `http://localhost:${config.server.port}`}/webhook/github`;
src/server.js:436:    const webhookSecret = config.github.webhookSecret;
src/server.js:437:    
src/server.js:438:    if (!webhookSecret) {
src/server.js:439:      return res.status(500).json({ error: 'Webhook secret not configured on server' });
src/server.js:440:    }
src/server.js:441:    
src/server.js:442:    const webhookResult = await githubAuth.createWebhook(githubUserId, repoFullName, webhookUrl, webhookSecret);
src/server.js:443:    
src/server.js:444:    const success = database.enableRepo(`github:${githubUserId}`, repoFullName);
src/server.js:445:    
src/server.js:446:    if (!success) {
src/server.js:447:      return res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to enable repo' });
src/server.js:448:    }
src/server.js:449:    
src/server.js:450:    console.log(`✅ Enabled repo ${repoFullName} for user github:${githubUserId}`);
src/server.js:451:    res.json({ 
src/server.js:452:      success: true, 
src/server.js:453:      repoFullName, 
src/server.js:454:      enabled: true,
src/server.js:455:      webhookCreated: !webhookResult.alreadyExists,
src/server.js:456:      webhookExists: webhookResult.alreadyExists
src/server.js:457:    });
src/server.js:458:  } catch (err) {
src/server.js:459:    console.error('❌ Failed to enable repo:', err);
src/server.js:460:    if (err.message === 'No valid access token available') {
src/server.js:461:      return res.status(401).json({ error: 'token_expired', message: 'Please sign in again.' });
src/server.js:462:    }

src/server.js:464:  }
src/server.js:465:});

src/server.js:511:// Set OG post for user's repo
src/server.js:512:app.post('/api/me/repos/og-post', async (req, res) => {
src/server.js:513:  const githubUserId = getGithubUserIdFromCookie(req);
src/server.js:514:  
src/server.js:515:  if (!githubUserId) {
src/server.js:516:    return res.status(401).json({ error: 'Not authenticated' });

src/server.js:523:  }
src/server.js:524:  
src/server.js:525:  // Verify user has access to this repo (auto-refreshes token)
src/server.js:526:  try {
src/server.js:527:    const repos = await githubAuth.getUserRepos(githubUserId);
src/server.js:528:    const hasAccess = repos.some(r => r.full_name === repoFullName);
src/server.js:529:    
src/server.js:530:    if (!hasAccess) {
src/server.js:531:      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'You do not have access to this repository' });
src/server.js:532:    }
src/server.js:533:    
src/server.js:534:    // Set OG post

src/server.js:536:    
src/server.js:537:    if (!success) {

src/server.js:539:    }

src/server.js:541:    // Also associate repo with user
src/server.js:542:    if (githubUserId) {
src/server.js:543:      database.addUserRepo(`github:${githubUserId}`, repoFullName);
src/server.js:544:    }
src/server.js:545:    
src/server.js:546:    res.json({ success: true, repoFullName, tweetId });
src/server.js:547:  } catch (err) {

src/server.js:549:    if (err.message === 'No valid access token available') {
src/server.js:550:      return res.status(401).json({ error: 'token_expired', message: 'Please sign in again.' });
src/server.js:551:    }

src/server.js:553:  }
